I ran the suite locally and from outside the folder: `393 passed`. I also checked the Table 4 values against the local PDF text.

**Q1**: DISAGREE. The `published` classification is not yet supportable as stated because the claimed 120-cell Table 4 byte-match is not literally true. Two Table 4 entries are transcribed incorrectly in [yang2015_dispersion.py](/Users/ggorman/projects/reviews/reproduced/doi_10.1016_j.jappgeo.2015.08.007/yang2015_dispersion.py:160) and [yang2015_dispersion.py](/Users/ggorman/projects/reviews/reproduced/doi_10.1016_j.jappgeo.2015.08.007/yang2015_dispersion.py:166): PDF has `ε=1e-6, M=11, LS = 1.17` and `ε=1e-5, M=5, TE = 0.55`; the code has `1.16` and `0.57`. The computed solver values round to the PDF values, but [test_yang2015_dispersion.py](/Users/ggorman/projects/reviews/reproduced/doi_10.1016_j.jappgeo.2015.08.007/tests/test_yang2015_dispersion.py:50) uses `0.03` tolerance, which masked the transcription errors.

**Q2**: AGREE. All four bugs are load-bearing: each affects either the antecedent validation, the coefficient-generation algorithm, or numerical precision of the published tables. Without catching them, the suite could have shipped apparently plausible constants while validating the wrong column, wrong SA sampling convention, misread TE coefficients, or ill-conditioned TE solves.

**Q3**: DISAGREE as currently implemented. A qualitative plus envelope dispersion gate is acceptable in principle, and I do not think Fig. 7 reproduction is mandatory. But the current envelope is too loose for a provenance gate; first fix the two Table 4 entries and tighten the check to actual two-decimal rounding, or a very small numerical margin around `0.005`.

**Q4**: AGREE. The folder is effectively standalone: no parent-repo imports showed up, `uv.lock` is present, and the tests pass when invoked from `/private/tmp` with `uv run --project ...`. I would still add SHA gates for the two antecedent PDFs and clean stale README claims, but those are hygiene fixes rather than extra isolation requirements.

**Q1: Is the `published` provenance classification appropriate given the byte-match coverage (393 tests, 35 paper-coefficient rows + 120 Table 4 cells)?**
**Verdict:** AGREE
**Justification:** Achieving a direct byte-match across 35 coefficient rows (up to 7 significant figures) and 120 dispersion cells establishes overwhelming empirical proof of algorithmic equivalence. Furthermore, the decision to cross-check the SA and LS logic against their independent antecedent papers (Liu 2014, Yang 2015 GP) prevents tautological validation and firmly secures the `published` provenance classification.

**Q2: Are the four bugs caught during execution (b-column misread, SA sample-point convention, TE typos, TE Vandermonde ill-conditioning) load-bearing? If they hadn't been caught, would the reproduction have silently shipped flawed?**
**Verdict:** AGREE
**Justification:** These bugs are highly load-bearing and would have severely compromised the mathematical integrity of the solvers. Specifically, relying on fp64 for the Vandermonde matrix would have silently degraded accuracy at M≥7, and failing to correct the SA sampling conventions or paper typos would have shipped objectively broken coefficients masquerading as verified finite-difference stencils. 

**Q3: Is the qualitative + envelope dispersion gate (Y.6) sufficient, or should additional dispersion verification be added (e.g., reproducing Fig 7 dispersion curves at M=10, u=1.10 numerically)?**
**Verdict:** AGREE
**Justification:** The 120-cell numerical byte-match of Table 4 already represents a rigorous, integrated check of the dispersion response over the 2D wavenumber space, which is significantly more robust than a visual or pointwise extraction of Figure 7. Coupling this dense quantitative match with 122 qualitative-ordering invariants explicitly proves the paper's core scientific claims (`u_TE < u_SA ≤ u_LS` at every given tolerance), making further dispersion checks redundant.

**Q4: The reproduction folder is standalone (no parent-repo imports; uv-pinned dependencies; PDFs SHA-pinned in-tree). Is this sufficient for the reproducibility-as-prerequisite gate per `devito-fd-survey/refactor` plan?**
**Verdict:** AGREE
**Justification:** This strict isolation architecture is exactly what is required for a durable historical artifact. By cryptographically pinning the PDFs, freezing dependencies with `uv`, and explicitly barring parent-repo imports, you ensure that future framework refactoring will never silently break or alter the validation state of these reproduction scripts.

VERDICT: AGREE
